max-height:1px; border-top:2px solid transparent; border-left:1px solid transparent;">\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Ozone\n       </b>\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="/o\xca\x8a/: \'o\' in \'code\'">\n            o\xca\x8a\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'z\' in \'zoom\'">\n            z\n           </span>\n           <span title="/o\xca\x8a/: \'o\' in \'code\'">\n            o\xca\x8a\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">\n            n\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       (systematically named\n       <b>\n        2\xce\xbb\n        <sup>\n         4\n        </sup>\n        -trioxidiene\n       </b>\n       and\n       <b>\n        <i>\n         catena\n        </i>\n        -trioxygen\n       </b>\n       ), or\n       <b>\n        trioxygen\n       </b>\n       , is an inorganic\n       <a href="/wiki/Molecule" title="Molecule">\n        molecule\n       </a>\n       with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chemical_formula" title="Chemical formula">\n        chemical formula\n       </a>\n       <b>\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n       </b>\n       . It is a pale blue gas with a distinctively\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pungent" title="Pungent">\n        pungent\n       </a>\n       smell. It is an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allotrope" title="Allotrope">\n        allotrope\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">\n        oxygen\n       </a>\n       that is much less stable than the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diatomic" title="Diatomic">\n        diatomic\n       </a>\n       allotrope\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        O\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       , breaking down in the lower atmosphere to\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        O\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dioxygen" title="Dioxygen">\n        dioxygen\n       </a>\n       . Ozone is formed from dioxygen by the action of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet" title="Ultraviolet">\n        ultraviolet\n       </a>\n       light and also atmospheric electrical discharges, and is present in very low concentrations throughout the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth%27s_atmosphere" title="Earth\'s atmosphere">\n        Earth\'s atmosphere\n       </a>\n       (stratosphere). Its concentration is highest in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ozone_layer" title="Ozone layer">\n        ozone layer\n       </a>\n       region of the atmosphere, which absorbs most of the Sun\'s ultraviolet (UV) radiation.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ozone\'s odour is sharp, reminiscent of chlorine, and detectable by many people at concentrations of as little as\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">\n         6993100000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0\n        </span>\n        100\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parts_per_billion" title="Parts per billion">\n         ppb\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       in air\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="No evidence for claim (February 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       . Ozone\'s O\n       <sub>\n        3\n       </sub>\n       structure was determined in 1865. The molecule was later proven to have a bent structure and to be\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diamagnetic" title="Diamagnetic">\n        diamagnetic\n       </a>\n       . In\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_conditions" title="Standard conditions">\n        standard conditions\n       </a>\n       , ozone is a pale blue gas that condenses at progressively cryogenic temperatures to a dark blue\n       <a href="/wiki/Liquid" title="Liquid">\n        liquid\n       </a>\n       and finally a violet-black\n       <a href="/wiki/Solid" title="Solid">\n        solid\n       </a>\n       . Ozone\'s instability with regard to more common dioxygen is such that both concentrated gas and liquid ozone may decompose explosively at elevated temperatures or fast warming to the boiling point.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-streng_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-streng-6">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is therefore used commercially only in low concentrations.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ozone is a powerful\n       <a href="/wiki/Oxidizing_agent" title="Oxidizing agent">\n        oxidant\n       </a>\n       (far more so than dioxygen) and has many industrial and consumer applications related to oxidation. This same high oxidising potential, however, causes ozone to damage mucous and respiratory tissues in animals, and also tissues in plants, above concentrations of about\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">\n         6993100000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0\n        </span>\n        100\xc2\xa0ppb\n       </span>\n       . This makes ozone a potent respiratory hazard and pollutant near ground level. However, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ozone_layer" title="Ozone layer">\n        ozone layer\n       </a>\n       (a portion of the stratosphere with a higher concentration of ozone, from two to eight ppm) is beneficial, preventing damaging\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultraviolet_light" title="Ultraviolet light">\n        ultraviolet light\n       </a>\n       from reaching the\n       <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">\n        Earth\n       </a>\n       \'s surface, to the benefit of both plants and animals.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#Nomenclature">\n     10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Applications\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36">\n           <a href="#Industry">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Industry\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37">\n           <a href="#Consumers">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Consumers\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38">\n           <a href="#Aquaculture">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Aquaculture\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-39">\n           <a href="#Agriculture">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Agriculture\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40">\n           <a href="#Medical">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.5\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Medical\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42">\n         <a href="#Notes">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           12\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Notes\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           13\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-44">\n         <a href="#Further_reading">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           14\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Further reading\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           15\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nomenclature">\n        Nomenclature\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Nomenclature">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Trivial_name" title="Trivial name">\n        trivial name\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        ozone\n       </i>\n       is the most commonly used and\n       <a href="/wiki/Preferred_IUPAC_name" title="Preferred IUPAC name">\n        preferred IUPAC name\n       </a>\n       . The systematic names\n       <i>\n        2\xce\xbb\n        <sup>\n         4\n        </sup>\n        -trioxidiene\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        catena-trioxygen\n       </i>\n       , valid\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IUPAC" title="IUPAC">\n        IUPAC\n       </a>\n       names, are constructed according to the substitutive and additive nomenclatures, respectively. The name\n       <i>\n        ozone\n       </i>\n       derives from\n       <i>\n        ozein\n       </i>\n       (\xe1\xbd\x84\xce\xb6\xce\xb5\xce\xb9\xce\xbd), the\n       <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">\n        Greek\n       </a>\n       verb for smell, referring to ozone\'s distinctive smell.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In appropriate contexts, ozone can be viewed as\n       <a href="/wiki/Trioxidane" title="Trioxidane">\n        trioxidane\n       </a>\n       with two hydrogen atoms removed, and as such,\n       <i>\n        trioxidanylidene\n       </i>\n       may be used as a context-specific systematic name, according to substitutive nomenclature. By default, these names pay no regard to the radicality of the ozone molecule. In even more specific context, this can also name the non-radical singlet ground state, whereas the diradical state is named\n       <i>\n        trioxidanediyl\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Trioxidanediyl\n       </i>\n       (or\n       <i>\n        ozonide\n       </i>\n       ) is used, non-systematically, to refer to the substituent group (-OOO-). Care should be taken to avoid confusing the name of the group for the context-specific name for ozone given above.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:213px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sch%C3%B6nbein.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="285" data-file-width="211" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e2/Sch%C3%B6nbein.jpg" width="211"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sch%C3%B6nbein.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Christian Friedrich Sch\xc3\xb6nbein (18 October 1799 \xe2\x80\x93 29 August 1868)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Smyths_revised_ozonometer,_1865._(9660571191).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1015" data-file-width="1250" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Smyths_revised_ozonometer%2C_1865._%289660571191%29.jpg/220px-Smyths_revised_ozonometer%2C_1865._%289660571191%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Smyths_revised_ozonometer%2C_1865._%289660571191%29.jpg/330px-Smyths_revised_ozonometer%2C_1865._%289660571191%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Smyths_revised_ozonometer%2C_1865._%289660571191%29.jpg/440px-Smyths_revised_ozonometer%2C_1865._%289660571191%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Smyths_revised_ozonometer,_1865._(9660571191).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A prototype ozonometer built by John Smyth in 1865\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1785, the Dutch chemist Martinus van Marum was conducting experiments involving electrical sparking above water when he noticed an unusual smell, which he attributed to the electrical reactions, failing to realize that he had in fact created ozone.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-colostate_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-colostate-7">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A half century later,\n       <a href="/wiki/Christian_Friedrich_Sch%C3%B6nbein" title="Christian Friedrich Sch\xc3\xb6nbein">\n        Christian Friedrich Sch\xc3\xb6nbein\n       </a>\n       noticed the same pungent odour and recognized it as the smell often following a bolt of\n       <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">\n        lightning\n       </a>\n       . In 1839, he succeeded in isolating the gaseous chemical and named it "ozone", from the Greek word\n       <i>\n        <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">\n         ozein\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       (\n       <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">\n        \xe1\xbd\x84\xce\xb6\xce\xb5\xce\xb9\xce\xbd\n       </span>\n       ) meaning "to smell".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ozo_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ozo-8">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For this reason, Sch\xc3\xb6nbein is generally credited with the discovery of ozone.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-colostate_7-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-colostate-7">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The formula for ozone, O\n       <sub>\n        3\n       </sub>\n       , was not determined until 1865 by\n       <a href="/wiki/Jacques-Louis_Soret" title="Jacques-Louis Soret">\n        Jacques-Louis Soret\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and confirmed by Sch\xc3\xb6nbein in 1867.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ozo_8-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ozo-8">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For much of the second half of the nineteenth century and well into the twentieth, ozone was considered a healthy component of the environment by naturalists and health-seekers.\n       <a href="/wiki/Beaumont,_California" title="Beaumont, California">\n        Beaumont\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">\n        California\n       </a>\n       had as its official slogan "Beaumont: Zone of Ozone", as evidenced on postcards and Chamber of Commerce letterhead.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Naturalists working outdoors often considered the higher elevations beneficial because of their ozone content. "There is quite a different atmosphere [at higher elevation] with enough ozone to sustain the necessary energy [to work]", wrote naturalist Henry Henshaw, working in Hawaii.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Seaside air was considered to be healthy because of its believed ozone content; but the smell giving rise to this belief is in fact that of halogenated seaweed metabolites.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ashfield_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ashfield-15">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In fact, even\n       <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin" title="Benjamin Franklin">\n        Benjamin Franklin\n       </a>\n       believed that the presence of cholera was connected with the deficiency or lack of ozone in the atmosphere, a sentiment shared by the\n       <a href="/wiki/British_Science_Association" title="British Science Association">\n        British Science Association\n       </a>\n       (then known simply as the British Association).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-franklin_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-franklin-16">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_properties">\n        Physical properties\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Physical properties">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Ozone is colourless or slightly bluish gas (blue when liquefied), slightly soluble in water and much more soluble in inert non-polar solvents such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_tetrachloride" title="Carbon tetrachloride">\n        carbon tetrachloride\n       </a>\n       or fluorocarbons, where it forms a blue solution. At 161\xc2\xa0K (\xe2\x88\x92112\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C; \xe2\x88\x92170\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F), it condenses to form a dark blue\n       <a href="/wiki/Liquid" title="Liquid">\n        liquid\n       </a>\n       . It is dangerous to allow this liquid to warm to its boiling point, because both concentrated gaseous ozone and liquid ozone can detonate. At temperatures below 80\xc2\xa0K (\xe2\x88\x92193.2\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C; \xe2\x88\x92315.7\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F), it forms a violet-black\n       <a href="/wiki/Solid" title="Solid">\n        solid\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Most people can detect about 0.01 \xce\xbcmol/mol of ozone in air where it has a very specific sharp odour somewhat resembling\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chlorine_bleach" title="Chlorine bleach">\n        chlorine bleach\n       </a>\n       . Exposure of 0.1 to 1 \xce\xbcmol/mol produces headaches, burning eyes and irritation to the respiratory passages.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brown_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-brown-18">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Even low concentrations of ozone in air are very destructive to organic materials such as latex, plastics and animal lung tissue.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ozone is\n       <a href="/wiki/Diamagnetism" title="Diamagnetism">\n        diamagnetic\n       </a>\n       , which means that its electrons are all paired. In contrast, O\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n       is\n       <a href="/wiki/Paramagnetism" title="Paramagnetism">\n        paramagnetic\n       </a>\n       , containing two unpaired electrons.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">\n        Structure\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Structure">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       According to experimental evidence from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microwave_spectroscopy" title="Microwave spectroscopy">\n        microwave spectroscopy\n       </a>\n       , ozone is a bent molecule, with C\n       <sub>\n        2v\n       </sub>\n       <a href="/wiki/Molecular_symmetry" title="Molecular symmetry">\n        symmetry\n       </a>\n       (similar to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">\n        water\n       </a>\n       molecule). The O \xe2\x80\x93 O distances are 127.2\n       <a href="/wiki/Picometre" title="Picometre">\n        pm\n       </a>\n       (1.272\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angstrom" title="Angstrom">\n        \xc3\x85\n       </a>\n       ). The O \xe2\x80\x93 O \xe2\x80\x93 O angle is 116.78\xc2\xb0.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The central atom is\n       <i>\n        sp\n       </i>\n       \xc2\xb2 hybridized with one lone pair. Ozone is a polar molecule with a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Molecular_dipole_moment" title="Molecular dipole moment">\n        dipole moment\n       </a>\n       of 0.53\n       <a href="/wiki/Debye" title="Debye">\n        D\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The molecule can be represented as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Resonance_(chemistry)" title="Resonance (chemistry)">\n        resonance\n       </a>\n       hybrid with two contributing structures, each with a\n       <a href="/wiki/Single_bond" title="Single bond">\n        single bond\n       </a>\n       on one side and\n       <a href="/wiki/Double_bond" title="Double bond">\n        double bond\n       </a>\n       on the other. The arrangement possesses an overall\n       <a href="/wiki/Bond_order" title="Bond order">\n        bond order\n       </a>\n       of 1.5 for both sides.\n      </p>\n      <center>\n       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ozone-resonance-Lewis-2D.png" title="Resonance Lewis structures of the ozone molecule">\n        <img alt="Resonance Lewis structures of the ozone molecule" data-file-height="295" data-file-width="1100" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Ozone-resonance-Lewis-2D.png/400px-Ozone-resonance-Lewis-2D.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Ozone-resonance-Lewis-2D.png/600px-Ozone-resonance-Lewis-2D.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Ozone-resonance-Lewis-2D.png/800px-Ozone-resonance-Lewis-2D.png 2x" width="400"/>\n       </a>\n      </center>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions">\n        Reactions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Reactions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Ozone is among the most powerful\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxidizing" title="Oxidizing">\n        oxidizing\n       </a>\n       agents known, far stronger than O\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n       . It is also unstable at high concentrations, decaying to ordinary diatomic oxygen. It has a varying\n       <a href="/wiki/Half-life" title="Half-life">\n        half-life\n       </a>\n       length, depending upon atmospheric conditions (temperature, humidity, and air movement). In a sealed chamber with a fan that moves the gas, ozone has a half-life of approximately a day at room temperature.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some unverified claims imply that ozone can have a half life as short as a half an hour under atmospheric conditions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        2\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 3\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       This reaction proceeds more rapidly with increasing temperature and increased pressure.\n       <a href="/wiki/Deflagration" title="Deflagration">\n        Deflagration\n       </a>\n       of ozone can be triggered by a spark, and can occur in ozone concentrations of 10\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wt%25" title="Wt%">\n        wt%\n       </a>\n       or higher.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ozone can also be produced electrochemically at the anode of an electrochemical cell from oxygen. This reaction can be used to create smaller quantities of ozone for research purposes.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        O\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         3\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       (g) + 2H\n       <sup>\n        +\n       </sup>\n       + 2e\n       <sup>\n        \xe2\x88\x92\n       </sup>\n       \xe2\x86\x90\xe2\x86\x92\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        O\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       (g) +\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        H\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n        O\n       </span>\n       E\xc2\xb0= 2.075V\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       This reaction can be observed as an unwanted reaction in a Hoffman gas apparatus during the electrolysis of water when the voltage is set above the necessary voltage.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="With_metals">\n        With metals\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: With metals">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Ozone will oxidise most\n       <a href="/wiki/Metal" title="Metal">\n        metals\n       </a>\n       (except\n       <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">\n        gold\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Platinum" title="Platinum">\n        platinum\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Iridium" title="Iridium">\n        iridium\n       </a>\n       ) to\n       <a href="/wiki/Oxide" title="Oxide">\n        oxides\n       </a>\n       of the metals in their highest\n       <a href="/wiki/Oxidation_state" title="Oxidation state">\n        oxidation state\n       </a>\n       . For example:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         Cu\n        </span>\n        +\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x86\x92\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         CuO\n        </span>\n        +\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="With_nitrogen_and_carbon_compounds">\n        With nitrogen and carbon compounds\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: With nitrogen and carbon compounds">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Ozone also oxidizes\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitric_oxide" title="Nitric oxide">\n        nitric oxide\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_dioxide" title="Nitrogen dioxide">\n        nitrogen dioxide\n       </a>\n       :\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        NO +\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x86\x92\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         NO\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        +\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       This reaction is accompanied by\n       <a href="/wiki/Chemiluminescence" title="Chemiluminescence">\n        chemiluminescence\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        NO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       can be further oxidized:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         NO\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        +\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x86\x92\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         NO\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        +\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        NO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         3\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       formed can react with\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        NO\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       to form\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        <a href="/wiki/Dinitrogen_pentoxide" title="Dinitrogen pentoxide">\n         N\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          5\n         </span>\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Solid\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitronium_perchlorate" title="Nitronium perchlorate">\n        nitronium perchlorate\n       </a>\n       can be made from NO\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n       , ClO\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n       , and\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        O\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         3\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       gases:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         NO\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        +\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         ClO\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        + 2\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x86\x92\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         NO\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n         ClO\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          4\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        + 2\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Ozone does not react with ammonium\n       <a href="/wiki/Salt" title="Salt">\n        salts\n       </a>\n       , but it oxidizes\n       <a href="/wiki/Ammonia" title="Ammonia">\n        ammonia\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Ammonium_nitrate" title="Ammonium nitrate">\n        ammonium nitrate\n       </a>\n       :\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        2\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         NH\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        + 4\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x86\x92\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         NH\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          4\n         </span>\n         NO\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        + 4\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        +\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         H\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n         O\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Ozone reacts with\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon" title="Carbon">\n        carbon\n       </a>\n       to form\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">\n        carbon dioxide\n       </a>\n       , even at room temperature:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        C + 2\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x86\x92\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         CO\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        + 2\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="With_sulfur_compounds">\n        With sulfur compounds\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: With sulfur compounds">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Ozone oxidises\n       <a href="/wiki/Sulfide" title="Sulfide">\n        sulfides\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Sulfate" title="Sulfate">\n        sulfates\n       </a>\n       . For example,\n       <a href="/wiki/Lead(II)_sulfide" title="Lead(II) sulfide">\n        lead(II) sulfide\n       </a>\n       is oxidised to\n       <a href="/wiki/Lead(II)_sulfate" title="Lead(II) sulfate">\n        lead(II) sulfate\n       </a>\n       :\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        PbS + 4 O\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 PbSO\n        <sub>\n         4\n        </sub>\n        + 4 O\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Sulfuric_acid" title="Sulfuric acid">\n        Sulfuric acid\n       </a>\n       can be produced from ozone, water and either elemental\n       <a href="/wiki/Sulfur" title="Sulfur">\n        sulfur\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">\n        sulfur dioxide\n       </a>\n       :\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        S + H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        O + O\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        SO\n        <sub>\n         4\n        </sub>\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        3 SO\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        + 3 H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        O + O\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 3 H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        SO\n        <sub>\n         4\n        </sub>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       In the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gas_phase" title="Gas phase">\n        gas phase\n       </a>\n       , ozone reacts with\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_sulfide" title="Hydrogen sulfide">\n        hydrogen sulfide\n       </a>\n       to form sulfur dioxide:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        S + O\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 SO\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        + H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        O\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       In an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aqueous" title="Aqueous">\n        aqueous\n       </a>\n       solution, however, two competing simultaneous reactions occur, one to produce elemental sulfur, and one to produce\n       <a href="/wiki/Sulfuric_acid" title="Sulfuric acid">\n        sulfuric acid\n       </a>\n       :\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        S + O\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 S + O\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        + H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        O\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        3 H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        S + 4 O\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 3 H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        SO\n        <sub>\n         4\n        </sub>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="With_alkenes_and_alkynes">\n        With alkenes and alkynes\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: With alkenes and alkynes">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Ozonolysis" title="Ozonolysis">\n        ozonolysis\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Alkenes can be oxidatively cleaved by ozone, in a process called\n       <a href="/wiki/Ozonolysis" title="Ozonolysis">\n        ozonolysis\n       </a>\n       , giving alcohols, aldehydes, ketones, and carboxylic acids, depending on the second step of the workup.\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ozonolysis_scheme.svg">\n         <img alt="Ozonolysis scheme.svg" data-file-height="134" data-file-width="515" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Ozonolysis_scheme.svg/515px-Ozonolysis_scheme.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Ozonolysis_scheme.svg/773px-Ozonolysis_scheme.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Ozonolysis_scheme.svg/1030px-Ozonolysis_scheme.svg.png 2x" width="515"/>\n        </a>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Ozone can also cleave alkynes to form a\n       <a href="/wiki/Acid_anhydride" title="Acid anhydride">\n        acid anhydride\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Diketone" title="Diketone">\n        diketone\n       </a>\n       product.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       If the reaction is performed in the presence of water, the anhydride hydrolyzes to give two\n       <a href="/wiki/Carboxylic_acid" title="Carboxylic acid">\n        carboxylic acids\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <div class="floatnone">\n         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ozonolysis-alkyne.png">\n          <img alt="Ozonolysis-alkyne.png" data-file-height="566" data-file-width="1349" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Ozonolysis-alkyne.png/450px-Ozonolysis-alkyne.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Ozonolysis-alkyne.png/675px-Ozonolysis-alkyne.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Ozonolysis-alkyne.png/900px-Ozonolysis-alkyne.png 2x" width="450"/>\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Usually ozonolysis is carried out in a solution of\n       <a href="/wiki/Dichloromethane" title="Dichloromethane">\n        dichloromethane\n       </a>\n       , at a temperature of \xe2\x88\x9278\n       <sup>\n        o\n       </sup>\n       C. After a sequence of cleavage and rearrangement, an organic ozonide is formed. With reductive workup (e.g.\n       <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">\n        zinc\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Acetic_acid" title="Acetic acid">\n        acetic acid\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Dimethyl_sulfide" title="Dimethyl sulfide">\n        dimethyl sulfide\n       </a>\n       ), ketones and aldehydes will be formed, with oxidative workup (e.g. aqueous or alcoholic\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_peroxide" title="Hydrogen peroxide">\n        hydrogen peroxide\n       </a>\n       ), carboxylic acids will be formed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OrgChem_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-OrgChem-26">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_substrates">\n        Other substrates\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Other substrates">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       All three\n       <a href="/wiki/Atom" title="Atom">\n        atoms\n       </a>\n       of ozone may also react, as in the reaction of\n       <a href="/wiki/Tin(II)_chloride" title="Tin(II) chloride">\n        tin(II) chloride\n       </a>\n       with\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrochloric_acid" title="Hydrochloric acid">\n        hydrochloric acid\n       </a>\n       and ozone:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        3 SnCl\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        + 6 HCl +\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 3 SnCl\n        <sub>\n         4\n        </sub>\n        + 3 H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        O\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Iodine perchlorate can be made by treating\n       <a href="/wiki/Iodine" title="Iodine">\n        iodine\n       </a>\n       dissolved in cold\n       <a href="/wiki/Anhydrous" title="Anhydrous">\n        anhydrous\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Perchloric_acid" title="Perchloric acid">\n        perchloric acid\n       </a>\n       with ozone:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        I\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        + 6 HClO\n        <sub>\n         4\n        </sub>\n        + O\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 2 I(ClO\n        <sub>\n         4\n        </sub>\n        )\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        + 3 H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        O\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Combustion">\n        Combustion\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Combustion">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Ozone can be used for\n       <a href="/wiki/Combustion" title="Combustion">\n        combustion\n       </a>\n       reactions and combustible gases; ozone provides higher temperatures than burning in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dioxygen" title="Dioxygen">\n        dioxygen\n       </a>\n       (O\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n       ). The following is a reaction for the combustion of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_subnitride" title="Carbon subnitride">\n        carbon subnitride\n       </a>\n       which can also cause higher temperatures:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        3\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         C\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          4\n         </span>\n         N\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        + 4\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 12 CO + 3\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         N\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Ozone can react at cryogenic temperatures. At 77\xc2\xa0K (\xe2\x88\x92196.2\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C; \xe2\x88\x92321.1\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F), atomic\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">\n        hydrogen\n       </a>\n       reacts with liquid ozone to form a hydrogen\n       <a href="/wiki/Superoxide" title="Superoxide">\n        superoxide\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Radical_(chemistry)" title="Radical (chemistry)">\n        radical\n       </a>\n       , which\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dimerizes" title="Dimerizes">\n        dimerizes\n       </a>\n       :\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Horvath_M._1985._pg_44_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Horvath_M._1985._pg_44-27">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        H +\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 HO\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        + O\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        2 HO\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        \xe2\x86\x92\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         H\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          4\n         </span>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Reduction_to_ozonides">\n        Reduction to ozonides\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Reduction to ozonides">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Reduction of ozone gives the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ozonide" title="Ozonide">\n        ozonide\n       </a>\n       anion, O\n       <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n        \xe2\x88\x92\n        <br/>\n        3\n       </span>\n       . Derivatives of this anion are explosive and must be stored at cryogenic temperatures. Ozonides for all the\n       <a href="/wiki/Alkali_metal" title="Alkali metal">\n        alkali metals\n       </a>\n       are known. KO\n       <sub>\n        3\n       </sub>\n       , RbO\n       <sub>\n        3\n       </sub>\n       , and CsO\n       <sub>\n        3\n       </sub>\n       can be prepared from their respective superoxides:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        KO\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        + O\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 KO\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        + O\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Although KO\n       <sub>\n        3\n       </sub>\n       can be formed as above, it can also be formed from\n       <a href="/wiki/Potassium_hydroxide" title="Potassium hydroxide">\n        potassium hydroxide\n       </a>\n       and ozone:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        2 KOH + 5 O\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 2 KO\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        + 5 O\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        + H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        O\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       NaO\n       <sub>\n        3\n       </sub>\n       and LiO\n       <sub>\n        3\n       </sub>\n       must be prepared by action of CsO\n       <sub>\n        3\n       </sub>\n       in liquid NH\n       <sub>\n        3\n       </sub>\n       on an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ion_exchange_resin" title="Ion exchange resin">\n        ion exchange resin\n       </a>\n       containing Na\n       <sup>\n        +\n       </sup>\n       or Li\n       <sup>\n        +\n       </sup>\n       ions:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        CsO\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        + Na\n        <sup>\n         +\n        </sup>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 Cs\n        <sup>\n         +\n        </sup>\n        + NaO\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       A solution of\n       <a href="/wiki/Calcium" title="Calcium">\n        calcium\n       </a>\n       in ammonia reacts with ozone to give to ammonium ozonide and not calcium ozonide:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Horvath_M._1985._pg_44_27-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Horvath_M._1985._pg_44-27">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        3 Ca + 10 NH\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        + 6\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 Ca\xc2\xb76NH\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        + Ca(OH)\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        + Ca(NO\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        )\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        + 2 NH\n        <sub>\n         4\n        </sub>\n        O\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        + 2 O\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        + H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Applications">\n        Applications\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Applications">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Ozone can be used to remove\n       <a href="/wiki/Iron" title="Iron">\n        iron\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">\n        manganese\n       </a>\n       from\n       <a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">\n        water\n       </a>\n       , forming a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitate" title="Precipitate">\n        precipitate\n       </a>\n       which can be filtered:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        2 Fe\n        <sup>\n         2+\n        </sup>\n        + O\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        + 5 H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        O \xe2\x86\x92 2 Fe(OH)\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        (s) + O\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        + 4 H\n        <sup>\n         +\n        </sup>\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        2 Mn\n        <sup>\n         2+\n        </sup>\n        + 2 O\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        + 4 H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        O \xe2\x86\x92 2 MnO(OH)\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        (s) + 2 O\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        + 4 H\n        <sup>\n         +\n        </sup>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Ozone will also oxidize dissolved\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_sulfide" title="Hydrogen sulfide">\n        hydrogen sulfide\n       </a>\n       in water to\n       <a href="/wiki/Sulfurous_acid" title="Sulfurous acid">\n        sulfurous acid\n       </a>\n       :\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        3\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        + H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        S \xe2\x86\x92 3 H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        SO\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        + 3 O\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       These three reactions are central in the use of ozone based well water treatment.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ozone will also detoxify\n       <a href="/wiki/Cyanide" title="Cyanide">\n        cyanides\n       </a>\n       by converting them to\n       <a href="/wiki/Cyanate" title="Cyanate">\n        cyanates\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        CN\n        <sup>\n         \xe2\x88\x92\n        </sup>\n        + O\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        \xe2\x86\x92\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         CNO\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          \xe2\x88\x92\n          <br/>\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        + O\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Ozone will also completely decompose\n       <a href="/wiki/Urea" title="Urea">\n        urea\n       </a>\n       :\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        (NH\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        )\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        CO + O\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 N\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        + CO\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        + 2 H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        O\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spectroscopic_properties">\n        Spectroscopic properties\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Spectroscopic properties">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Ozone is a bent\n       <a href="/wiki/Triatomic_molecule" title="Triatomic molecule">\n        triatomic molecule\n       </a>\n       with three vibrational modes: the symmetric stretch (1103.157\xc2\xa0cm\n       <sup>\n        \xe2\x88\x921\n       </sup>\n       ), bend (701.42\xc2\xa0cm\n       <sup>\n        \xe2\x88\x921\n       </sup>\n       ) and antisymmetric stretch (1042.096\xc2\xa0cm\n       <sup>\n        \xe2\x88\x921\n       </sup>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The symmetric stretch and bend are weak absorbers, but the antisymmetric stretch is strong and responsible for ozone being an important minor\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">\n        greenhouse gas\n       </a>\n       . This IR band is also used to detect ambient and atmospheric ozone although UV based measurements are more common.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The electronic spectrum of ozone is quite complex. An overview can be seen at the MPI Mainz UV/VIS Spectral Atlas of Gaseous Molecules of Atmospheric Interest.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       All of the bands are dissociative, meaning that the molecule falls apart to\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        O + O\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n       </span>\n       after absorbing a photon. The most important absorption is the Hartley band, extending from slightly above 300\xc2\xa0nm down to slightly above 200\xc2\xa0nm. It is this band that is responsible for absorbing UV\xc2\xa0C in the stratosphere.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On the high wavelength side, the Hartley band transitions to the so-called Huggins band, which falls off rapidly until disappearing by ~360\xc2\xa0nm. Above 400\xc2\xa0nm, extending well out into the NIR, are the Chappius and Wulf bands. There, unstructured absorption bands are useful for detecting high ambient concentrations of ozone, but are so weak that they do not have much practical effect.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are additional absorption bands in the far UV, which increase slowly from 200\xc2\xa0nm down to reaching a maximum at ~120\xc2\xa0nm.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span id="Ozone_in_Earth\'s_atmosphere">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ozone_in_Earth.27s_atmosphere">\n        Ozone in Earth\'s atmosphere\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Ozone in Earth\'s atmosphere">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atmospheric_ozone.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="688" data-file-width="1162" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Atmospheric_ozone.svg/220px-Atmospheric_ozone.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Atmospheric_ozone.svg/330px-Atmospheric_ozone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Atmospheric_ozone.svg/440px-Atmospheric_ozone.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atmospheric_ozone.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The distribution of atmospheric ozone in partial pressure as a function of altitude\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nimbus_ozone_Brewer-Dobson_circulation.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="504" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Nimbus_ozone_Brewer-Dobson_circulation.jpg/220px-Nimbus_ozone_Brewer-Dobson_circulation.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Nimbus_ozone_Brewer-Dobson_circulation.jpg/330px-Nimbus_ozone_Brewer-Dobson_circulation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Nimbus_ozone_Brewer-Dobson_circulation.jpg/440px-Nimbus_ozone_Brewer-Dobson_circulation.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nimbus_ozone_Brewer-Dobson_circulation.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Concentration of ozone as measured by the\n         <a href="/wiki/Nimbus_program" title="Nimbus program">\n          Nimbus-7\n         </a>\n         satellite\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IM_ozavg_ept_200006.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/IM_ozavg_ept_200006.png/220px-IM_ozavg_ept_200006.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/IM_ozavg_ept_200006.png/330px-IM_ozavg_ept_200006.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/IM_ozavg_ept_200006.png/440px-IM_ozavg_ept_200006.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IM_ozavg_ept_200006.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Total ozone concentration in June 2000 as measured by EP-TOMS satellite instrument\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The standard way to express total ozone levels (the amount of ozone in a given vertical column) in the atmosphere is by using\n       <a href="/wiki/Dobson_unit" title="Dobson unit">\n        Dobson units\n       </a>\n       . Point measurements are reported as\n       <a href="/wiki/Mole_fraction" title="Mole fraction">\n        mole fractions\n       </a>\n       in nmol/mol (parts per billion, ppb) or as\n       <a href="/wiki/Concentration" title="Concentration">\n        concentrations\n       </a>\n       in \xce\xbcg/m\n       <sup>\n        3\n       </sup>\n       . The study of ozone concentration in the atmosphere started in the 1920s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ozone_layer">\n        Ozone layer\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ozone layer">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Ozone_layer" title="Ozone layer">\n        Ozone layer\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Location_and_production">\n        Location and production\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Location and production">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The highest levels of ozone in the atmosphere are in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Stratosphere" title="Stratosphere">\n        stratosphere\n       </a>\n       , in a region also known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ozone_layer" title="Ozone layer">\n        ozone layer\n       </a>\n       between about 10\xc2\xa0km and 50\xc2\xa0km above the surface (or between about 6 and 31 miles). However, even in this "layer", the ozone concentrations are only two to eight parts per million, so most of the oxygen there is dioxygen, O\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n       , at about 210,000 parts per million by volume.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ozone in the stratosphere is mostly produced from short-wave ultraviolet rays between 240 and 160\xc2\xa0nm. Oxygen starts to absorb weakly at 240\xc2\xa0nm in the Herzberg bands, but most of the oxygen is dissociated by absorption in the strong\n       <b>\n        <a href="/wiki/Schumann%E2%80%93Runge_bands" title="Schumann\xe2\x80\x93Runge bands">\n         Schumann\xe2\x80\x93Runge bands\n        </a>\n       </b>\n       between 200 and 160\xc2\xa0nm where ozone does not absorb. While shorter wavelength light, extending to even the X-Ray limit, is energetic enough to dissociate molecular oxygen, there is relatively little of it, and, the strong solar emission at Lyman-alpha, 121\xc2\xa0nm, falls at a point where molecular oxygen absorption is a minimum.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The process of ozone creation and destruction is called the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chapman_cycle" title="Chapman cycle">\n        Chapman cycle\n       </a>\n       and starts with the photolysis of molecular oxygen\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        +\n        <a href="/wiki/Photon" title="Photon">\n         photon\n        </a>\n        (radiation \xce\xbb &lt; 240 nm) \xe2\x86\x92 2 O\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       followed by reaction of the oxygen atom with another molecule of oxygen to form ozone.\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        O +\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        + M \xe2\x86\x92\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        + M\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       where "M" denotes the third body that carries off the excess energy of the reaction. The ozone molecule can then absorb a UV-C photon and dissociate\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        O\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         3\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x86\x92 O +\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        O\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       + kinetic energy\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The excess kinetic energy heats the stratosphere when the O atoms and the molecular oxygen fly apart and collide with other molecules. This conversion of UV light into kinetic energy warms the stratosphere. The oxygen atoms produced in the photolysis of ozone then react back with other oxygen molecule as in the previous step to form more ozone. In the clear atmosphere, with only nitrogen and oxygen, ozone can react with the atomic oxygen to form two molecules of O\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        + O \xe2\x86\x92 2\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       An estimate of the rate of this termination step to the cycling of atomic oxygen back to ozone can be found simply by taking the ratios of the concentration of O\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n       to O\n       <sub>\n        3\n       </sub>\n       . The termination reaction is\n       <a href="/wiki/Catalysis" title="Catalysis">\n        catalysed\n       </a>\n       by the presence of certain free radicals, of which the most important are hydroxyl (OH), nitric oxide (NO) and atomic chlorine (Cl) and bromine (Br). In the second half of the 20th Century the amount of ozone in the stratosphere was discovered to be declining, mostly because of increasing concentrations of\n       <a href="/wiki/Chlorofluorocarbon" title="Chlorofluorocarbon">\n        chlorofluorocarbons\n       </a>\n       (CFC) and similar\n       <a href="/wiki/Haloalkane" title="Haloalkane">\n        chlorinated and brominated organic molecules\n       </a>\n       . The concern over the health effects of the decline led to the 1987\n       <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Protocol" title="Montreal Protocol">\n        Montreal Protocol\n       </a>\n       , the ban on the production of many\n       <a href="/wiki/Ozone_depletion" title="Ozone depletion">\n        ozone depleting\n       </a>\n       chemicals and in the first and second decade of the 21st Century the beginning of the recovery of stratospheric ozone concentrations.\n      </p>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ozone-oxygen_cycle" title="Ozone-oxygen cycle">\n        Ozone-oxygen cycle\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ozone_depletion" title="Ozone depletion">\n        Ozone depletion\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Importance_to_surface-dwelling_life_on_Earth">\n        Importance to surface-dwelling life on Earth\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Importance to surface-dwelling life on Earth">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ozone_altitude_UV_graph.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="380" data-file-width="504" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Ozone_altitude_UV_graph.svg/220px-Ozone_altitude_UV_graph.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Ozone_altitude_UV_graph.svg/330px-Ozone_altitude_UV_graph.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Ozone_altitude_UV_graph.svg/440px-Ozone_altitude_UV_graph.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ozone_altitude_UV_graph.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Levels of ozone at various altitudes and blocking of different bands of ultraviolet radiation. Essentially all UVC (100\xe2\x80\x93280\xc2\xa0nm) is blocked by dioxygen (at 100\xe2\x80\x93200\xc2\xa0nm) or by ozone (at 200\xe2\x80\x93280\xc2\xa0nm) in the atmosphere. The shorter portion of this band and even more energetic UV causes the formation of the ozone layer, when single oxygen atoms produced by UV\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Photolysis" title="Photolysis">\n          photolysis\n         </a>\n         of dioxygen (below 240\xc2\xa0nm) react with more dioxygen.
