The ozone layer itself then blocks most, but not quite all, sunburn-producing UVB (280\xe2\x80\x93315\xc2\xa0nm). The band of UV closest to visible light, UVA (315\xe2\x80\x93400\xc2\xa0nm), is hardly affected by ozone, and most of it reaches the ground.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Ozone in the ozone layer filters out sunlight wavelengths from about 200\xc2\xa0nm UV rays to 315\xc2\xa0nm, with ozone peak absorption at about 250\xc2\xa0nm.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This ozone UV absorption is important to life, since it extends the absorption of UV by ordinary oxygen and nitrogen in air (which absorb all wavelengths &lt; 200\xc2\xa0nm) through the lower UV-C (200\xe2\x80\x93280\xc2\xa0nm) and the entire UV-B band (280\xe2\x80\x93315\xc2\xa0nm). The small unabsorbed part that remains of UV-B after passage through ozone causes sunburn in humans, and direct DNA damage in living tissues in both plants and animals. Ozone\'s effect on mid-range UV-B rays is illustrated by its effect on UV-B at 290\xc2\xa0nm, which has a radiation intensity 350 million times as powerful at the top of the atmosphere as at the surface. Nevertheless, enough of UV-B radiation at similar frequency reaches the ground to cause some sunburn, and these same wavelengths are also among those responsible for the production of\n       <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_D" title="Vitamin D">\n        vitamin D\n       </a>\n       in humans.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The ozone layer has little effect on the longer UV wavelengths called UV-A (315\xe2\x80\x93400\xc2\xa0nm), but this radiation does not cause sunburn or direct DNA damage, and while it probably does cause long-term skin damage in certain humans, it is not as dangerous to plants and to the health of surface-dwelling organisms on Earth in general (see\n       <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet" title="Ultraviolet">\n        ultraviolet\n       </a>\n       for more information on near ultraviolet).\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Low_level_ozone">\n        Low level ozone\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Low level ozone">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropospheric_ozone" title="Tropospheric ozone">\n        Tropospheric ozone\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Photochemical_smog" title="Photochemical smog">\n        Photochemical smog\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Low level ozone (or tropospheric ozone) is an atmospheric pollutant.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-who-Europe_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-who-Europe-37">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is not emitted directly by\n       <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">\n        car engines\n       </a>\n       or by industrial operations, but formed by the reaction of sunlight on air containing\n       <a href="/wiki/Volatile_organic_compound" title="Volatile organic compound">\n        hydrocarbons\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide" title="Nitrogen oxide">\n        nitrogen oxides\n       </a>\n       that react to form ozone directly at the source of the pollution or many kilometers down wind.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ozone reacts directly with some hydrocarbons such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Aldehyde" title="Aldehyde">\n        aldehydes\n       </a>\n       and thus begins their removal from the air, but the products are themselves key components of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Photochemical_smog" title="Photochemical smog">\n        smog\n       </a>\n       . Ozone\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Photolysis" title="Photolysis">\n        photolysis\n       </a>\n       by UV light leads to production of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydroxyl_radical" title="Hydroxyl radical">\n        hydroxyl radical\n       </a>\n       HO\xe2\x80\xa2 and this plays a part in the removal of hydrocarbons from the air, but is also the first step in the creation of components of smog such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Peroxyacyl_nitrates" title="Peroxyacyl nitrates">\n        peroxyacyl nitrates\n       </a>\n       , which can be powerful eye irritants. The atmospheric lifetime of tropospheric ozone is about 22 days; its main removal mechanisms are being deposited to the ground, the above-mentioned reaction giving HO\xe2\x80\xa2, and by reactions with OH and the peroxy radical HO\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n       \xe2\x80\xa2.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There is evidence of significant reduction in agricultural yields because of increased ground-level ozone and pollution which interferes with\n       <a href="/wiki/Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis">\n        photosynthesis\n       </a>\n       and stunts overall growth of some plant species.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arb.ca.gov_40-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-arb.ca.gov-40">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">\n        United States Environmental Protection Agency\n       </a>\n       is proposing a secondary regulation to reduce crop damage, in addition to the primary regulation designed for the protection of human health.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Certain examples of cities with elevated ozone readings are\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houston,_Texas" title="Houston, Texas">\n        Houston, Texas\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">\n        Mexico City\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">\n        Mexico\n       </a>\n       . Houston has a reading of around 41 nmol/mol, while Mexico City is far more hazardous, with a reading of about 125 nmol/mol.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arb.ca.gov_40-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-arb.ca.gov-40">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ozone_cracking">\n        Ozone cracking\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ozone cracking">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ozone_cracks_in_tube1.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="270" data-file-width="510" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6a/Ozone_cracks_in_tube1.jpg/220px-Ozone_cracks_in_tube1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6a/Ozone_cracks_in_tube1.jpg/330px-Ozone_cracks_in_tube1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6a/Ozone_cracks_in_tube1.jpg/440px-Ozone_cracks_in_tube1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ozone_cracks_in_tube1.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Ozone cracking in\n         <a href="/wiki/Natural_rubber" title="Natural rubber">\n          natural rubber\n         </a>\n         tubing\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Ozone gas attacks any\n       <a href="/wiki/Polymer" title="Polymer">\n        polymer\n       </a>\n       possessing olefinic or\n       <a href="/wiki/Double_bond" title="Double bond">\n        double bonds\n       </a>\n       within its chain structure, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_rubber" title="Natural rubber">\n        natural rubber\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitrile_rubber" title="Nitrile rubber">\n        nitrile rubber\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Styrene-butadiene" title="Styrene-butadiene">\n        styrene-butadiene\n       </a>\n       rubber. Products made using these polymers are especially susceptible to attack, which causes cracks to grow longer and deeper with time, the rate of crack growth depending on the load carried by the rubber component and the concentration of ozone in the atmosphere. Such materials can be protected by adding\n       <a href="/wiki/Antiozonant" title="Antiozonant">\n        antiozonants\n       </a>\n       , such as waxes, which bond to the surface to create a protective film or blend with the material and provide long term protection.\n       <a href="/wiki/Ozone_cracking" title="Ozone cracking">\n        Ozone cracking\n       </a>\n       used to be a serious problem in car tires for example, but the problem is now seen only in very old tires.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">\n          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2012)">\n           clarification needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2012)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       On the other hand, many critical products, like\n       <a href="/wiki/Gasket" title="Gasket">\n        gaskets\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/O-ring" title="O-ring">\n        O-rings\n       </a>\n       , may be attacked by ozone produced within compressed air systems.\n       <a href="/wiki/Fuel_line" title="Fuel line">\n        Fuel lines\n       </a>\n       made of reinforced rubber are also susceptible to attack, especially within the engine compartment, where some ozone is produced by electrical components. Storing rubber products in close proximity to a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct_Current" title="Direct Current">\n        DC\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">\n        electric motor\n       </a>\n       can accelerate ozone cracking. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Commutator_(electric)" title="Commutator (electric)">\n        commutator\n       </a>\n       of the motor generates sparks which in turn produce ozone.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ozone_as_a_greenhouse_gas">\n        Ozone as a greenhouse gas\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Ozone as a greenhouse gas">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Although ozone was present at ground level before the\n       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">\n        Industrial Revolution\n       </a>\n       , peak concentrations are now far higher than the pre-industrial levels, and even background concentrations well away from sources of pollution are substantially higher.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ozone acts as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">\n        greenhouse gas\n       </a>\n       , absorbing some of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Infrared" title="Infrared">\n        infrared\n       </a>\n       energy emitted by the earth. Quantifying the greenhouse gas potency of ozone is difficult because it is not present in uniform concentrations across the globe. However, the most widely accepted scientific assessments relating to\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">\n        climate change\n       </a>\n       (e.g. the\n       <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">\n        Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_Assessment_Report" title="Third Assessment Report">\n        Third Assessment Report\n       </a>\n       )\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       suggest that the\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiative_forcing" title="Radiative forcing">\n        radiative forcing\n       </a>\n       of tropospheric ozone is about 25% that of\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">\n        carbon dioxide\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The annual\n       <a href="/wiki/Global_warming_potential" title="Global warming potential">\n        global warming potential\n       </a>\n       of tropospheric ozone is between 918\xe2\x80\x931022 tons\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_equivalent" title="Carbon dioxide equivalent">\n        carbon dioxide equivalent\n       </a>\n       /tons tropospheric ozone. This means on a per-molecule basis, ozone in the troposphere has a\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiative_forcing" title="Radiative forcing">\n        radiative forcing\n       </a>\n       effect roughly 1,000 times as strong as\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">\n        carbon dioxide\n       </a>\n       . However, tropospheric ozone is a short-lived\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">\n        greenhouse gas\n       </a>\n       , which decays in the atmosphere much more quickly than\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">\n        carbon dioxide\n       </a>\n       . This means that over a 20-year span, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Global_warming_potential" title="Global warming potential">\n        global warming potential\n       </a>\n       of tropospheric ozone is much less, roughly 62 to 69 tons\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_equivalent" title="Carbon dioxide equivalent">\n        carbon dioxide equivalent\n       </a>\n       / ton tropospheric ozone.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Because of its short-lived nature, tropospheric ozone does not have strong global effects, but has very strong radiative forcing effects on regional scales. In fact, there are regions of the world where tropospheric ozone has a\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiative_forcing" title="Radiative forcing">\n        radiative forcing\n       </a>\n       up to 150% of\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">\n        carbon dioxide\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health_effects">\n        Health effects\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Health effects">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_the_coal_industry" title="Environmental impact of the coal industry">\n        Environmental impact of the coal industry\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ozone_air_pollution">\n        Ozone air pollution\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Ozone air pollution">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alder_showing_ozone_discolouration.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="240" data-file-width="350" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Alder_showing_ozone_discolouration.jpg/220px-Alder_showing_ozone_discolouration.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Alder_showing_ozone_discolouration.jpg/330px-Alder_showing_ozone_discolouration.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/46/Alder_showing_ozone_discolouration.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alder_showing_ozone_discolouration.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Alnus_rubra" title="Alnus rubra">\n          Red Alder\n         </a>\n         leaf, showing discolouration caused by ozone pollution\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EONASA_46-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-EONASA-46">\n           [45]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SignboardAirQualityHouston.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/SignboardAirQualityHouston.JPG/220px-SignboardAirQualityHouston.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/SignboardAirQualityHouston.JPG/330px-SignboardAirQualityHouston.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/SignboardAirQualityHouston.JPG/440px-SignboardAirQualityHouston.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SignboardAirQualityHouston.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Signboard in\n         <a href="/wiki/Gulfton,_Houston" title="Gulfton, Houston">\n          Gulfton\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">\n          Houston\n         </a>\n         indicating an ozone watch\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Ozone precursors are a group of pollutants, predominantly those emitted during the combustion of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels" title="Fossil fuels">\n        fossil fuels\n       </a>\n       . Ground-level ozone pollution (\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropospheric_ozone" title="Tropospheric ozone">\n        tropospheric ozone\n       </a>\n       ) is created near the Earth\'s surface by the action of daylight\n       <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet" title="Ultraviolet">\n        UV\n       </a>\n       rays on these precursors. The ozone at ground level is primarily from fossil fuel precursors, but\n       <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">\n        methane\n       </a>\n       is a natural precursor, and the very low natural background level of ozone at ground level is considered safe. This section examines the health impacts of fossil fuel burning, which raises ground level ozone far above background levels.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There is a great deal of evidence to show that ground-level ozone can harm lung function and irritate the\n       <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_system" title="Respiratory system">\n        respiratory system\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-who-Europe_37-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-who-Europe-37">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Exposure to ozone (and the pollutants that produce it) is linked to premature\n       <a href="/wiki/Death" title="Death">\n        death\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Asthma" title="Asthma">\n        asthma\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bronchitis" title="Bronchitis">\n        bronchitis\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heart_attack" title="Heart attack">\n        heart attack\n       </a>\n       , and other cardiopulmonary problems.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid18629332_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pmid18629332-49">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Long-term exposure to ozone has been shown to increase risk of death from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Respiratory_illness" title="Respiratory illness">\n        respiratory illness\n       </a>\n       . A study of 450,000 people living in United States cities saw a significant correlation between ozone levels and respiratory illness over the 18-year follow-up period. The study revealed that people living in cities with high ozone levels, such as Houston or Los Angeles, had an over 30% increased risk of dying from lung disease.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Air quality guidelines such as those from the\n       <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">\n        World Health Organization\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">\n        United States Environmental Protection Agency\n       </a>\n       (EPA) and the\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">\n        European Union\n       </a>\n       are based on detailed studies designed to identify the levels that can cause measurable ill\n       <a href="/wiki/Health_effect" title="Health effect">\n        health effects\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to scientists with the US EPA, susceptible people can be adversely affected by ozone levels as low as 40 nmol/mol.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid18629332_49-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pmid18629332-49">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the EU, the current target value for ozone concentrations is 120\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb5g/m\n       <sup>\n        3\n       </sup>\n       which is about 60 nmol/mol. This target applies to all member states in accordance with Directive 2008/50/EC.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ozone concentration is measured as a maximum daily mean of 8 hour averages and the target should not be exceeded on more than 25 calendar days per year, starting from January 2010. Whilst the directive requires in the future a strict compliance with 120\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb5g/m\n       <sup>\n        3\n       </sup>\n       limit (i.e. mean ozone concentration not to be exceeded on any day of the year), there is no date set for this requirement and this is treated as a long-term objective.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the USA, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Clean_Air_Act_(United_States)" title="Clean Air Act (United States)">\n        Clean Air Act\n       </a>\n       directs the EPA to set\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Ambient_Air_Quality_Standards" title="National Ambient Air Quality Standards">\n        National Ambient Air Quality Standards\n       </a>\n       for several pollutants, including ground-level ozone, and counties out of compliance with these standards are required to take steps to reduce their levels. In May 2008, under a court order, the EPA lowered its ozone standard from 80 nmol/mol to 75 nmol/mol. The move proved controversial, since the Agency\'s own scientists and advisory board had recommended lowering the standard to 60 nmol/mol.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid18629332_49-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pmid18629332-49">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Many public health and environmental groups also supported the 60 nmol/mol standard,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">\n        World Health Organization\n       </a>\n       recommends 51 nmol/mol.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On January 7, 2010, the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) announced proposed revisions to the National Ambient Air Quality Standard (NAAQS) for the pollutant ozone, the principal component of smog:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        ... EPA proposes that the level of the 8-hour primary standard, which was set at 0.075 \xce\xbcmol/mol in the 2008 final rule, should instead be set at a lower level within the range of 0.060 to 0.070 \xce\xbcmol/mol, to provide increased protection for children and other \xe2\x80\x98\xe2\x80\x98at risk\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x99 populations against an array of\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 related adverse health effects that range from decreased lung function and increased respiratory symptoms to serious indicators of respiratory morbidity including emergency department visits and hospital admissions for respiratory causes, and possibly cardiovascular-related morbidity as well as total non- accidental and cardiopulmonary mortality....\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n         <a href="#cite_note-57">\n          [56]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       On October 26, 2015, the EPA published a final rule with an effective date of December 28, 2015 that revised the 8-hour primary NAAQS from 0.075 ppm to 0.070 ppm.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The EPA has developed an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_Quality_Index" title="Air Quality Index">\n        Air Quality Index\n       </a>\n       (AQI) to help explain air pollution levels to the general public. Under the current standards, eight-hour average ozone mole fractions of 85 to 104 nmol/mol are described as "unhealthy for sensitive groups", 105 nmol/mol to 124 nmol/mol as "unhealthy", and 125 nmol/mol to 404 nmol/mol as "very unhealthy".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ozone can also be present in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indoor_air_pollution" title="Indoor air pollution">\n        indoor air pollution\n       </a>\n       , partly as a result of electronic equipment such as photocopiers. A connection has also been known to exist between the increased pollen, fungal spores, and ozone caused by thunderstorms and hospital admissions of\n       <a href="/wiki/Asthma" title="Asthma">\n        asthma\n       </a>\n       sufferers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the\n       <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">\n        Victorian era\n       </a>\n       , one British folk myth held that the smell of the sea was caused by ozone. In fact, the characteristic "smell of the sea" is caused by\n       <a href="/wiki/Dimethyl_sulfide" title="Dimethyl sulfide">\n        dimethyl sulfide\n       </a>\n       , a chemical generated by\n       <a href="/wiki/Phytoplankton" title="Phytoplankton">\n        phytoplankton\n       </a>\n       . Victorian British folk considered the resulting smell "bracing".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Heat_waves">\n        Heat waves\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Heat waves">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Ozone production rises during heat waves, because plants absorb less ozone. It is estimated that curtailed ozone absorption by plants was responsible for the loss of 460 lives in the UK in the hot summer of 2006.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A similar investigation to assess the joint effects of ozone and heat during the European heat waves in 2003, concluded that these appear to be additive.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Physiology">\n        Physiology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Physiology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Trioxidane" title="Trioxidane">\n        Trioxidane\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Ozone, along with reactive forms of oxygen such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Superoxide" title="Superoxide">\n        superoxide\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Singlet_oxygen" title="Singlet oxygen">\n        singlet oxygen\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_peroxide" title="Hydrogen peroxide">\n        hydrogen peroxide\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hypochlorite" title="Hypochlorite">\n        hypochlorite\n       </a>\n       ions, is naturally produced by\n       <a href="/wiki/White_blood_cell" title="White blood cell">\n        white blood cells\n       </a>\n       and other biological systems (such as the roots of\n       <a href="/wiki/Tagetes" title="Tagetes">\n        marigolds\n       </a>\n       ) as a means of destroying foreign bodies. Ozone reacts directly with organic double bonds. Also, when ozone breaks down to dioxygen it gives rise to oxygen\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_radical" title="Free radical">\n        free radicals\n       </a>\n       , which are highly reactive and capable of damaging many\n       <a href="/wiki/Organic_compound" title="Organic compound">\n        organic molecules\n       </a>\n       . Moreover, it is believed that the powerful oxidizing properties of ozone may be a contributing factor of\n       <a href="/wiki/Inflammation" title="Inflammation">\n        inflammation\n       </a>\n       . The cause-and-effect relationship of how the ozone is created in the body and what it does is still under consideration and still subject to various interpretations, since other body chemical processes can trigger some of the same reactions. A team headed by Paul Wentworth Jr. of the Department of Chemistry at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Scripps_Research_Institute" title="Scripps Research Institute">\n        Scripps Research Institute\n       </a>\n       has shown evidence linking the antibody-catalyzed water-oxidation pathway of the human\n       <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">\n        immune response\n       </a>\n       to the production of ozone. In this system, ozone is produced by antibody-catalyzed production of\n       <a href="/wiki/Trioxidane" title="Trioxidane">\n        trioxidane\n       </a>\n       from water and neutrophil-produced singlet oxygen.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       When inhaled, ozone reacts with compounds lining the lungs to form specific, cholesterol-derived metabolites that are thought to facilitate the build-up and pathogenesis of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atherosclerotic_plaques" title="Atherosclerotic plaques">\n        atherosclerotic plaques\n       </a>\n       (a form of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heart_disease" title="Heart disease">\n        heart disease\n       </a>\n       ). These metabolites have been confirmed as naturally occurring in human atherosclerotic arteries and are categorized into a class of secosterols termed\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Atheronals" title="Atheronals">\n         atheronals\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , generated by\n       <a href="/wiki/Ozonolysis" title="Ozonolysis">\n        ozonolysis\n       </a>\n       of cholesterol\'s double bond to form a\n       <a href="/wiki/Atheronals" title="Atheronals">\n        5,6 secosterol\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       as well as a secondary condensation product via aldolization.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ozone has been implicated to have an adverse effect on plant growth: "... ozone reduced total chlorophylls, carotenoid and carbohydrate concentration, and increased 1-aminocyclopropane-1-carboxylic acid (ACC) content and ethylene production. In treated plants, the ascorbate leaf pool was decreased, while lipid peroxidation and solute leakage were significantly higher than in ozone-free controls. The data indicated that ozone triggered protective mechanisms against oxidative stress in citrus."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Safety_regulations">\n        Safety regulations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Safety regulations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Because of the strongly oxidizing properties of ozone, ozone is a primary irritant, affecting especially the eyes and respiratory systems and can be hazardous at even low concentrations. The Canadian Centre for Occupation Safety and Health reports that:\n      </p>\n      <blockquote>\n       <p>\n        "Even very low concentrations of ozone can be harmful to the upper respiratory tract and the lungs. The severity of injury depends on both by the concentration of ozone and the duration of exposure. Severe and permanent lung injury or death could result from even a very short-term exposure to relatively low concentrations."\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n         <a href="#cite_note-68">\n          [67]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </p>\n      </blockquote>\n      <p>\n       To protect workers potentially exposed to ozone,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Occupational_Safety_and_Health_Administration" title="U.S. Occupational Safety and Health Administration">\n        U.S. Occupational Safety and Health Administration\n       </a>\n       has established a permissible exposure limit (PEL) of 0.1 \xce\xbcmol/mol (29 CFR 1910.1000 table Z-1), calculated as an 8-hour time weighted average. Higher concentrations are especially hazardous and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NIOSH" title="NIOSH">\n        NIOSH\n       </a>\n       has established an Immediately Dangerous to Life and Health Limit (IDLH) of 5 \xce\xbcmol/mol.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Work environments where ozone is used or where it is likely to be produced should have adequate ventilation and it is prudent to have a monitor for ozone that will alarm if the concentration exceeds the OSHA PEL. Continuous monitors for ozone are available from several suppliers.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Elevated ozone exposure can occur on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Passenger_aircraft" title="Passenger aircraft">\n        passenger aircraft\n       </a>\n       , with levels depending on altitude and atmospheric turbulence.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portfolio_70-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-portfolio-70">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       United States\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Authority" title="Federal Aviation Authority">\n        Federal Aviation Authority\n       </a>\n       regulations set a limit of 250 nmol/mol with a maximum four-hour average of 100 nmol/mol.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some planes are equipped with ozone converters in the ventilation system to reduce passenger exposure.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-portfolio_70-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-portfolio-70">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Production">\n        Production\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Production">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:THC_2003.902.021_E._H._Johnson_Ozone_Production.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2941" data-file-width="3139" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/THC_2003.902.021_E._H._Johnson_Ozone_Production.jpg/220px-THC_2003.902.021_E._H._Johnson_Ozone_Production.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/THC_2003.902.021_E._H._Johnson_Ozone_Production.jpg/330px-THC_2003.902.021_E._H._Johnson_Ozone_Production.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/THC_2003.902.021_E._H._Johnson_Ozone_Production.jpg/440px-THC_2003.902.021_E._H._Johnson_Ozone_Production.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:THC_2003.902.021_E._H._Johnson_Ozone_Production.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Ozone production demonstration, Fixed Nitrogen Research Laboratory, 1926\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Ozone generators are used to produce ozone for cleaning air or removing smoke odours\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in unoccupied rooms. These ozone generators can produce over 3 g of ozone per hour. Ozone often forms in nature under conditions where O\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n       will not react.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brown_18-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-brown-18">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ozone used in industry is measured in \xce\xbcmol/mol (ppm, parts per million), nmol/mol (ppb, parts per billion), \xce\xbcg/m\n       <sup>\n        3\n       </sup>\n       , mg/h (milligrams per hour) or weight percent. The regime of applied concentrations ranges from 1% to 5% (in air) and from 6% to 14% (in oxygen) for older generation methods. New electrolytic methods can achieve up 20% to 30% dissolved ozone concentrations in output water.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Temperature and humidity play a large role in how much ozone is being produced using traditional generation methods (such as corona discharge and ultraviolet light). Old generation methods will produce less than 50% of nominal capacity if operated with humid ambient air, as opposed to very dry air. New generators, using electrolytic methods, can achieve higher purity and dissolution through using water molecules as the source of ozone production.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Corona_discharge_method">\n        Corona discharge method\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Corona discharge method">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       This is the most common type of ozone generator for most industrial and personal uses. While variations of the "hot spark" coronal discharge method of ozone production exist, including medical grade and industrial grade ozone generators, these units usually work by means of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Corona_discharge" title="Corona discharge">\n        corona discharge tube\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They are typically cost-effective and do not require an oxygen source other than the ambient air to produce ozone concentrations of 3\xe2\x80\x936%. Fluctuations in ambient air, due to weather or other environmental conditions, cause variability in ozone production. However, they also produce\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide" title="Nitrogen oxide">\n        nitrogen oxides\n       </a>\n       as a by-product. Use of an\n       <a href="/wiki/Air_dryer" title="Air dryer">\n        air dryer\n       </a>\n       can reduce or eliminate nitric acid formation by removing water vapor and increase ozone production. Use of an\n       <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_concentrator" title="Oxygen concentrator">\n        oxygen concentrator\n       </a>\n       can further increase the ozone production and further reduce the risk of nitric acid formation by removing not only the water vapor, but also the bulk of the nitrogen.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ultraviolet_light">\n        Ultraviolet light\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Ultraviolet light">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       UV ozone generators, or vacuum-ultraviolet (VUV) ozone generators, employ a light source that generates a narrow-band ultraviolet light, a subset of that produced by the Sun. The Sun\'s UV sustains the ozone layer in the stratosphere of Earth.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       UV ozone generators use ambient air for ozone production, no air prep systems are used (air dryer or oxygen concentrator), therefore these generators tend to be less expensive. However UV ozone generators usually produce ozone with a concentration of about 0.5% or lower which limits the potential ozone production rate. Another disadvantage of this method is that it requires the ambient air (oxygen) to be exposed to the UV source for a longer amount of time, and any gas that is not exposed to the UV source will not be treated. This makes UV generators impractical for use in situations that deal with rapidly moving air or water streams (in-duct air\n       <a href="/wiki/Sterilization_(microbiology)" title="Sterilization (microbiology)">\n        sterilization\n       </a>\n       , for example). Production of ozone is one of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet_germicidal_irradiation#Potential_dangers" title="Ultraviolet germicidal irradiation">\n        potential dangers\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet_germicidal_irradiation" title="Ultraviolet germicidal irradiation">\n        ultraviolet germicidal irradiation\n       </a>\n       . VUV ozone generators are used in swimming pool and\n       <a href="/wiki/Spa" title="Spa">\n        spa\n       </a>\n       applications ranging to millions of gallons of water. VUV ozone generators, unlike corona discharge generators, do not produce harmful nitrogen by-products and also unlike corona discharge systems, VUV ozone generators work extremely well in humid air environments. There is also not normally a need for expensive off-gas mechanisms, and no need for air driers or oxygen concentrators which require extra costs and maintenance.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_plasma">\n        Cold plasma\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Cold plasma">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In the cold plasma method, pure oxygen gas is exposed to a\n       <a href="/wiki/Plasma_(physics)" title="Plasma (physics)">\n        plasma\n       </a>\n       created by\n       <a href="/wiki/Dielectric_barrier_discharge" title="Dielectric barrier discharge">\n        dielectric barrier discharge\n       </a>\n       . The diatomic oxygen is split into single atoms, which then recombine in triplets to form ozone.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Cold plasma machines utilize pure oxygen as the input source and produce a maximum concentration of about 5% ozone. They produce far greater quantities of ozone in a given space of time compared to ultraviolet production. However, because cold plasma ozone generators are very expensive, they are found less frequently than the previous two types.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The discharges manifest as filamentary transfer of electrons (micro discharges) in a gap between two electrodes. In order to evenly distribute the micro discharges, a dielectric\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrical_insulation" title="Electrical insulation">\n        insulator\n       </a>\n       must be used to separate the metallic electrodes and to prevent arcing.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Some cold plasma units also have the capability of producing short-lived allotropes of oxygen which include O\n       <sub>\n        4\n       </sub>\n       , O\n       <sub>\n        5\n       </sub>\n       , O\n       <sub>\n        6\n       </sub>\n       , O\n       <sub>\n        7\n       </sub>\n       , etc. These species are even more reactive than ordinary\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        O\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         3\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Electrolytic">\n        Electrolytic\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Electrolytic">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Electrolytic ozone generation (EOG) splits water molecules into H\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n       , O\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n       , and O\n       <sub>\n        3\n       </sub>\n       . In most EOG methods, the hydrogen gas will be removed to leave oxygen and ozone as the only reaction products. Therefore, EOG can achieve higher\n       <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_(chemistry)" title="Dissolution (chemistry)">\n        dissolution\n       </a>\n       in water without other competing gases found in corona discharge method, such as nitrogen gases present in ambient air. This method of generation can achieve concentrations of 20\xe2\x80\x9330% and is independent of air quality because water is used as the source material. Production of ozone electrolytically is typically unfavorable because of the high\n       <a href="/wiki/Overpotential" title="Overpotential">\n        overpotential\n       </a>\n       required to produce ozone as compared to oxygen. This is why ozone is not produced during typical water electrolysis. However, it is possible to increase the overpotential of oxygen by careful catalyst selection such that ozone is preferentially produced under electrolysis. Catalysts typically chosen for this approach are\n       <a href="/wiki/Lead_dioxide" title="Lead dioxide">\n        lead dioxide\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       or boron-doped diamond.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Special_considerations">\n        Special considerations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Special considerations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Ozone cannot be stored and transported like other industrial gases (because it quickly decays into diatomic oxygen) and must therefore be produced on site. Available ozone generators vary in the arrangement and design of the high-voltage electrodes. At production capacities higher than 20\xc2\xa0kg per hour, a gas/water tube heat-exchanger may be utilized as ground electrode and assembled with tubular high-voltage electrodes on the gas-side. The regime of typical gas pressures is around 2\n       <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">\n        bars\n       </a>\n       (200\n       <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">\n        kPa\n       </a>\n       ) absolute in oxygen and 3 bars (300\xc2\xa0kPa) absolute in air. Several megawatts of\n       <a href="/wiki/Electric_power" title="Electric power">\n        electrical power\n       </a>\n       may be installed in large facilities, applied as one phase AC\n       <a href="/wiki/Electric_current" title="Electric current">\n        current\n       </a>\n       at 50 to 8000\xc2\xa0Hz and peak\n       <a href="/wiki/Voltage" title="Voltage">\n        voltages\n       </a>\n       between 3,000 and 20,000 volts. Applied voltage is usually inversely related to the applied frequency.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The dominating parameter influencing ozone generation efficiency is the gas temperature, which is controlled by cooling water temperature and/or gas velocity. The cooler the water, the better the ozone synthesis. The lower the gas velocity, the higher the concentration (but the lower the net ozone produced). At typical industrial conditions, almost 90% of the effective power is dissipated as heat and needs to be removed by a sufficient cooling water flow.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Because of the high reactivity of ozone, only a few materials may be used like\n       <a href="/wiki/Stainless_steel" title="Stainless steel">\n        stainless steel\n       </a>\n       (quality 316L),\n       <a href="/wiki/Titanium" title="Titanium">\n        titanium\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Aluminium" title="Aluminium">\n        aluminium\n       </a>\n       (as long as no moisture is present),\n       <a href="/wiki/Glass" title="Glass">\n        glass\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polytetrafluorethylene" title="Polytetrafluorethylene">\n        polytetrafluorethylene\n       </a>\n       , or\n       <a href="/wiki/Polyvinylidene_fluoride" title="Polyvinylidene fluoride">\n        polyvinylidene fluoride\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Viton" title="Viton">\n        Viton\n       </a>\n       may be used with the restriction of constant mechanical forces and absence of humidity (humidity limitations apply depending on the formulation).\n       <a href="/wiki/Hypalon" title="Hypalon">\n        Hypalon\n       </a>\n       may be used with the restriction that no water come in contact with it, except for normal atmospheric levels.\n       <a href="/wiki/Embrittlement" title="Embrittlement">\n        Embrittlement\n       </a>\n       or shrinkage is the common mode of failure of elastomers with exposure to ozone. Ozone cracking is the common mode of failure of elastomer seals like\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/O-rings" title="O-rings">\n        O-rings\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Silicone_rubber" title="Silicone rubber">\n        Silicone rubbers\n       </a>\n       are usually adequate for use as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaskets" title="Gaskets">\n        gaskets\n       </a>\n       in ozone concentrations below 1 wt%, such as in equipment for accelerated aging of rubber samples.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Incidental_production">\n        Incidental production\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Incidental production">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Ozone may be formed from\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        O\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       by electrical discharges and by action of high energy\n       <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_radiation" title="Electromagnetic radiation">\n        electromagnetic radiation\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Arc_suppression" title="Arc suppression">\n        Unsuppressed arcing\n       </a>\n       in electrical contacts, motor brushes, or mechanical switches breaks down the chemical bonds of the atmospheric oxygen surrounding the contacts [\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        O\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       \xe2\x86\x92 2O]. Free radicals of oxygen in and around the arc recombine to create ozone [\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        O\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         3\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       ].\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n        <a href="#cite_note-78">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Certain\n       <a href="/wiki/Electrical_equipment" title="Electrical equipment">\n        electrical equipment\n       </a>\n       generate significant levels of ozone. This is especially true of devices using\n       <a href="/wiki/High_voltage" title="High voltage">\n        high voltages\n       </a>\n       , such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Air_ioniser" title="Air ioniser">\n        ionic air purifiers\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laser_printer" title="Laser printer">\n        laser printers\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Photocopier" title="Photocopier">\n        photocopiers\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Electroshock_weapon" title="Electroshock weapon">\n        tasers\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Arc_welding" title="Arc welding">\n        arc welders\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">\n        Electric motors\n       </a>\n       using\n       <a href="/wiki/Brush_(electric)" title="Brush (electric)">\n        brushes\n       </a>\n       can generate ozone from repeated\n       <a href="/wiki/Spark_gap" title="Spark gap">\n        sparking\n       </a>\n       inside the unit. Large motors that use brushes, such as those used by elevators or hydraulic pumps, will generate more ozone than smaller motors.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ozone is similarly formed in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Catatumbo_lightning" title="Catatumbo lightning">\n        Catatumbo lightning storms\n       </a>\n       phenomenon on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Catatumbo_River" title="Catatumbo River">\n        Catatumbo River\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">\n        Venezuela\n       </a>\n       , though ozone\'s instability makes it dubious that it has any effect on the ozonosphere.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zulia_79-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Zulia-79">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is the world\'s largest single natural generator of ozone, lending calls for it to be designated a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">\n        UNESCO World Heritage Site\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-meteo_80-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-meteo-80">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Laboratory_production">\n        Laboratory production\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Laboratory production">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In the laboratory, ozone can be produced by\n       <a href="/wiki/Electrolysis" title="Electrolysis">\n        electrolysis\n       </a>\n       using a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/9_volt_battery" title="9 volt battery">\n        9 volt battery\n       </a>\n       , a pencil graphite rod\n       <a href="/wiki/Cathode" title="Cathode">\n        cathode\n       </a>\n       , a\n       <a href="/wiki/Platinum" title="Platinum">\n        platinum\n       </a>\n       wire\n       <a href="/wiki/Anode" title="Anode">\n        anode\n       </a>\n       and a 3\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Molar_(concentration)" title="Molar (concentration)">\n        molar\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Sulfuric_acid" title="Sulfuric acid">\n        sulfuric acid\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Electrolyte" title="Electrolyte">\n        electrolyte\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n        <a href="#cite_note-81">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Half_cell" title="Half cell">\n        half cell\n       </a>\n       reactions taking place are:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        3 H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        O \xe2\x86\x92 O\n        <sub>\n         3\n        </sub>\n        + 6 H\n        <sup>\n         +\n        </sup>\n        + 6 e\n        <sup>\n         \xe2\x88\x92\n        </sup>\n        (\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Table_of_standard_electrode_potentials" title="Table of standard electrode potentials">\n         \xce\x94E\n         <sup>\n          o\n         </sup>\n        </a>\n        = \xe2\x88\x921.53\n        <a href="/wiki/Volt" title="Volt">\n         V\n        </a>\n        )\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        6 H\n        <sup>\n         +\n        </sup>\n        + 6 e\n        <sup>\n         \xe2\x88\x92\n        </sup>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 3 H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        (\xce\x94E\n        <sup>\n         o\n        </sup>\n        = 0 V)\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        2 H\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        O \xe2\x86\x92 O\n        <sub>\n         2\n        </sub>\n        + 4 H\n        <sup>\n         +\n        </sup>\n        + 4 e\n        <sup>\n         \xe2\x88\x92\n        </sup>\n        (\xce\x94E\n        <sup>\n         o\n        </sup>\n        = 1.23 V)\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       In the net reaction, three equivalents of water are converted into one equivalent of ozone and three equivalents of\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">\n        hydrogen\n       </a>\n       . Oxygen formation is a competing reaction.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It can also be generated by a\n       <a href="/wiki/High_voltage" title="High voltage">\n        high voltage\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Electric_arc" title="Electric arc">\n        arc\n       </a>\n       . In its simplest form, high voltage AC, such as the output of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Neon-sign_transformer" title="Neon-sign transformer">\n        Neon-sign transformer\n       </a>\n       is connected to two metal rods with the ends placed sufficiently close to each other to allow an arc. The resulting arc will convert atmospheric oxygen to ozone.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It is often desirable to contain the ozone. This can be done with an apparatus consisting of two concentric glass tubes sealed together at the top with gas ports at the top and bottom of the outer tube. The inner core should have a length of metal foil inserted into it connected to one side of the power source. The other side of the power source should be connected to another piece of foil wrapped around the outer tube. A source of dry\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        O\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       is applied to the bottom port. When high voltage is applied to the foil leads,\n       <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">\n        electricity\n       </a>\n       will discharge between the dry dioxygen in the middle and form\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        O\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         3\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="chemf nowrap">\n        O\n        <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n         <br/>\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       which will flow out the top port. The reaction can be summarized as follows:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brown_18-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-brown-18">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        3\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <i>\n         electricity\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x86\x92 2\n        <span class="chemf nowrap">\n         O\n         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">\n          <br/>\n          3\n         </span>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Applications_2">\n        Applications\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Applications">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">\n        Industry\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Industry">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The largest use of ozone is in the preparation of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pharmaceuticals" title="Pharmaceuticals">\n        pharmaceuticals\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synthetic_lubricants" title="Synthetic lubricants">\n        synthetic lubricants\n       </a>\n       , and many other commercially useful\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organic_compounds" title="Organic compounds">\n        organic compounds\n       </a>\n       , where it is used to sever\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon" title="Carbon">\n        carbon\n       </a>\n       -carbon bonds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brown_18-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-brown-18">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It can also be used for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bleach_(chemical)" title="Bleach (chemical)">\n        bleaching\n       </a>\n       substances and for killing microorganisms in air and water sources.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n        <a href="#cite_note-82">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Many municipal drinking water systems kill bacteria with ozone instead of the more common\n       <a href="/wiki/Chlorine" title="Chlorine">\n        chlorine\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n        <a href="#cite_note-83">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ozone has a very high\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxidation_potential" title="Oxidation potential">\n        oxidation potential\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ozone does not form\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organochlorine" title="Organochlorine">\n        organochlorine\n       </a>\n       compounds, nor does it remain in the water after treatment. Ozone can form the suspected carcinogen\n       <a href="/wiki/Bromate" title="Bromate">\n        bromate\n       </a>\n       in source water with high\n       <a href="/wiki/Bromide" title="Bromide">\n        bromide\n       </a>\n       concentrations. The U.S.\n       <a href="/wiki/Safe_Drinking_Water_Act" title="Safe Drinking Water Act">\n        Safe Drinking Water Act\n       </a>\n       mandates that these systems introduce an amount of chlorine to maintain a minimum of 0.2 \xce\xbcmol/mol residual\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_chlorine" title="Free chlorine">\n        free chlorine\n       </a>\n       in the pipes, based on results of regular testing. Where\n       <a href="/wiki/Electric_power" title="Electric power">\n        electrical power\n       </a>\n       is abundant, ozone is a cost-effective method of treating water, since it is produced on demand and does not require transportation and storage of hazardous chemicals. Once it has decayed, it leaves no taste or odour in drinking water.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Although low levels of ozone have been advertised to be of some disinfectant use in residential homes, the concentration of ozone in dry air required to have a rapid, substantial effect on airborne pathogens exceeds safe levels recommended by the U.S.\n       <a href="/wiki/Occupational_Safety_and_Health_Administration" title="Occupational Safety and Health Administration">\n        Occupational Safety and Health Administration\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="Environmental Protection Agency">\n        Environmental Protection Agency\n       </a>\n       . Humidity control can vastly improve both the killing power of the ozone and the rate at which it decays back to oxygen (more humidity allows more effectiveness).\n       <a href="/wiki/Spore" title="Spore">\n        Spore\n       </a>\n       forms of most pathogens are very tolerant of atmospheric ozone in concentrations where asthma patients start to have issues.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Industrially, ozone is used to:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Disinfect laundry in hospitals, food factories, care homes etc.;\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n         <a href="#cite_note-85">\n          [84]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Disinfect water in place of chlorine\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brown_18-4">\n         <a href="#cite_note-brown-18">\n          [17]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deodorize" title="Deodorize">\n         Deodorize\n        </a>\n        air and objects, such as after a fire. This process is extensively used in\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fabric_restoration" title="Fabric restoration">\n         fabric restoration\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Kill bacteria on food or on contact surfaces;\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-food_86-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-food-86">\n          [85]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Sanitize swimming pools and spas\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Kill insects in stored grain\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">\n         <a href="#cite_note-87">\n          [86]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Scrub yeast and mold spores from the air in food processing plants;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Wash fresh fruits and vegetables to kill yeast, mold and bacteria;\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-food_86-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-food-86">\n          [85]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Chemically attack contaminants in water (\n        <a href="/wiki/Iron" title="Iron">\n         iron\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Arsenic" title="Arsenic">\n         arsenic\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_sulfide" title="Hydrogen sulfide">\n         hydrogen sulfide\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Nitrite" title="Nitrite">\n         nitrites\n        </a>\n        , and complex organics lumped together as "colour");\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Provide an aid to\n        <a href="/wiki/Flocculation" title="Flocculation">\n         flocculation\n        </a>\n        (agglomeration of molecules, which aids in filtration, where the iron and arsenic are removed);\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Manufacture chemical compounds via chemical synthesis\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n         <a href="#cite_note-88">\n          [87]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Clean and bleach fabrics (the former use is utilized in fabric restoration; the latter use is patented);\n        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n         [\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2012)">\n            citation needed\n           </span>\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         ]\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Act as an\n        <a href="/wiki/Antichlor" title="Antichlor">\n         antichlor\n        </a>\n        in chlorine-based bleaching;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Assist in processing plastics to allow adhesion of inks;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Age rubber samples to determine the useful life of a batch of rubber;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Eradicate water borne parasites such as\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Giardia_lamblia" title="Giardia lamblia">\n          Giardia lamblia\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        and\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Cryptosporidium" title="Cryptosporidium">\n          Cryptosporidium\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        in surface water treatment plants.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Ozone is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Reagent" title="Reagent">\n        reagent\n       </a>\n       in many\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organic_reactions" title="Organic reactions">\n        organic reactions\n       </a>\n       in the laboratory and in industry.\n       <a href="/wiki/Ozonolysis" title="Ozonolysis">\n        Ozonolysis\n       </a>\n       is the cleavage of an\n       <a href="/wiki/Alkene" title="Alkene">\n        alkene\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbonyl" title="Carbonyl">\n        carbonyl\n       </a>\n       compounds.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Many hospitals around the world use large ozone generators to decontaminate operating rooms between surgeries. The rooms are cleaned and then sealed airtight before being filled with ozone which effectively kills or neutralizes all remaining bacteria.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ozone is used as an alternative to\n       <a href="/wiki/Chlorine" title="Chlorine">\n        chlorine\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Chlorine_dioxide" title="Chlorine dioxide">\n        chlorine dioxide\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bleaching_of_wood_pulp" title="Bleaching of wood pulp">\n        bleaching of wood pulp\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">\n        <a href="#cite_note-90">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is often used in conjunction with oxygen and hydrogen peroxide to eliminate the need for chlorine-containing compounds in the manufacture of high-quality, white\n       <a href="/wiki/Paper" title="Paper">\n        paper\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ozone can be used to detoxify\n       <a href="/wiki/Cyanide" title="Cyanide">\n        cyanide\n       </a>\n       wastes (for example from\n       <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">\n        gold\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Silver" title="Silver">\n        silver\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">\n        mining\n       </a>\n       ) by oxidising cyanide to\n       <a href="/wiki/Cyanate" title="Cyanate">\n        cyanate\n       </a>\n       and eventually to\n       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">\n        carbon dioxide\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Consumers">\n        Consumers\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ozone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Consumers">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Air_purifier#Potential_ozone_hazards"
